/></a></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>The <b>University of Washington</b> (commonly referred to as <b>UW</b>, simply <b>Washington</b>, or informally <b>"U-Dub"</b>)<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> is a large, public flagship research university in <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>, established in 1861.</p>\n<p>Washington is one of the oldest universities on the West Coast. It has three campuses, with the oldest and largest being located in the <a href="/wiki/University_District,_Seattle" title="University District, Seattle">University District</a> of Seattle and two others in <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_Tacoma" title="University of Washington Tacoma">Tacoma</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_Bothell" title="University of Washington Bothell">Bothell</a>. The university is among the most reputable and most competitive within the United States. Overall, Washington encompasses 500 buildings and over 20 million gross square footage of space, including over 26 university libraries, the <a href="/wiki/UW_Tower" title="UW Tower">UW Tower</a> office building, art centers, museums, lecture halls, laboratories and conference centers.</p>\n<p>Washington is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> and is consistently ranked among the top 15 universities in the world by a variety of international publications. The University offers bachelor\'s, master\'s and doctoral degrees through its 140 departments, organized into various colleges and schools. Its alumni, faculty and students include <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> laureates, <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners, Fulbright Scholars, Rhodes Scholars, Marshall Scholars, as well as members of distinguished institutions. Washington is home to the best <a href="/wiki/Medical_school" title="Medical school">medical school</a> in the U.S.,<sup id="cite_ref-USNWR_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNWR-6">[6]</a></sup> as well as some of the nation\'s top schools in <a href="/wiki/Business_school" title="Business school">business</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Law_school" title="Law school">law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pharmacy_school" title="Pharmacy school">pharmacy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Statistics" title="Statistics">statistics</a>. In athletics, the university competes in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" class="mw-redirect" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> <a href="/wiki/Pac-12_Conference" title="Pac-12 Conference">Pac-12 Conference</a> (Pac-12). Its athletic teams are called the Huskies.</p>\n<p></p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Support"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Support</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-20"><a href="#Housing"><span class="tocnumber">5.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Housing</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-21"><a href="#Disabilities"><span class="tocnumber">5.3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Disabilities</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Athletics"><span class="tocnumber">5.4</span> <span class="toctext">Athletics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-23"><a href="#Husky_Stadium"><span class="tocnumber">5.4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Husky Stadium</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-24"><a href="#Mascot"><span class="tocnumber">5.4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Mascot</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Song"><span class="tocnumber">5.5</span> <span class="toctext">Song</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Notable_alumni_and_faculty"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Notable alumni and faculty</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#In_film"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">In film</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:238px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Territorial_University_of_Washington_-_c1870.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/df/Territorial_University_of_Washington_-_c1870.jpg/236px-Territorial_University_of_Washington_-_c1870.jpg" width="236" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/df/Territorial_University_of_Washington_-_c1870.jpg/354px-Territorial_University_of_Washington_-_c1870.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/df/Territorial_University_of_Washington_-_c1870.jpg/472px-Territorial_University_of_Washington_-_c1870.jpg 2x" data-file-width="550" data-file-height="410" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Territorial_University_of_Washington_-_c1870.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe original University building, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 1870</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding">Founding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Founding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1854, territorial governor <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Stevens" title="Isaac Stevens">Isaac Stevens</a> recommended the establishment of a university in <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>. Prominent Seattle-area residents, including <a href="/wiki/Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist">Methodist</a> preacher Daniel Bagley, saw this as a chance to add to the city\'s potential and prestige. They convinced early founder of Seattle (and member of the territorial legislature), <a href="/wiki/Arthur_A._Denny" title="Arthur A. Denny">Arthur A. Denny</a>, on the importance of the school. Two universities were initially chartered, but later the decision was repealed in favor of a single university in <a href="/wiki/Lewis_County,_Washington" title="Lewis County, Washington">Lewis County</a> provided that locally donated land was available. When no site emerged, Denny successfully petitioned the legislature to reconsider Seattle as a location in 1858.</p>\n<p>In 1861, scouting began for an appropriate 10 acres (4&#160;ha) site in Seattle to serve as a new university campus. Arthur and Mary Denny donated eight acres, while fellow pioneers Edward Lander, and Charlie and Mary Terry, donated two acres on Denny\'s Knoll in <a href="/wiki/Downtown,_Seattle,_Washington" class="mw-redirect" title="Downtown, Seattle, Washington">downtown Seattle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bhatt_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bhatt-7">[7]</a></sup> More specifically, this tract was bounded by 4th Avenue to the west, 6th Avenue to the east, Union Street to the north, and Seneca Streets to the south.</p>\n<p>On November 4, 1861, Washington opened as the <a href="/wiki/Territorial_University_of_Washington" class="mw-redirect" title="Territorial University of Washington">Territorial University of Washington</a>. The legislature passed articles incorporating the university, and establishing its Board of Regents in 1862. The school initially struggled, closing three times: in 1863 for low enrollment and again in 1867 and 1876 due to funds shortage. Washington successfully awarded its first graduate <a href="/wiki/Clara_Antoinette_McCarty_Wilt" title="Clara Antoinette McCarty Wilt">Clara Antoinette McCarty Wilt</a> in 1876, with a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor\'s degree">bachelor\'s degree</a> in science.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century_relocation">19th century relocation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 19th century relocation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>By the time <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington State</a> entered the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">Union</a> in 1889, both Seattle and the University had grown substantially. Washington\'s total undergraduate enrollment increased from 30 to nearly 300 students, and the campus\'s relative isolation in downtown Seattle faced encroaching development. A special legislative committee, headed by UW graduate <a href="/wiki/Edmond_Meany" class="mw-redirect" title="Edmond Meany">Edmond Meany</a>, was created to find a new campus to better serve the growing student population and faculty. The committee eventually selected a site on the northeast of <a href="/wiki/Downtown,_Seattle,_Washington" class="mw-redirect" title="Downtown, Seattle, Washington">downtown Seattle</a>, called <a href="/wiki/Union_Bay_(Seattle,_Washington)" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Bay (Seattle, Washington)">Union Bay</a>, and the legislature appropriated funds for its purchase and construction.</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:238px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alaska_Yukon_Pacific_Exposition_-_Rainier_Vista.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Alaska_Yukon_Pacific_Exposition_-_Rainier_Vista.jpg/236px-Alaska_Yukon_Pacific_Exposition_-_Rainier_Vista.jpg" width="236" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Alaska_Yukon_Pacific_Exposition_-_Rainier_Vista.jpg/354px-Alaska_Yukon_Pacific_Exposition_-_Rainier_Vista.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Alaska_Yukon_Pacific_Exposition_-_Rainier_Vista.jpg/472px-Alaska_Yukon_Pacific_Exposition_-_Rainier_Vista.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="480" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alaska_Yukon_Pacific_Exposition_-_Rainier_Vista.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nAlaska-Yukon-Pacific Exposition on the UW campus toward <a href="/wiki/Mount_Rainier" title="Mount Rainier">Mount Rainier</a> in 1909</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In 1895, the university relocated to the new campus by moving into the newly built <a href="/wiki/Denny_Hall" title="Denny Hall">Denny Hall</a>. The University Regents tried and failed to sell the old campus, eventually settling with leasing the area. This would later become one of the University\'s most valuable pieces of real estate in modern-day Seattle, generating millions in annual revenue with what is now called the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Tract_(Seattle)" title="Metropolitan Tract (Seattle)">Metropolitan Tract</a>. The original Territorial University building was torn down in 1908, and its former site now houses the <a href="/wiki/Fairmont_Olympic_Hotel" class="mw-redirect" title="Fairmont Olympic Hotel">Fairmont Olympic Hotel</a>.</p>\n<p>The sole-surviving remnants of Washington\'s first building are four 24-foot (7.3&#160;m), white, hand-fluted cedar, Ionic columns. They were salvaged by <a href="/wiki/Edmond_S._Meany" title="Edmond S. Meany">Edmond S. Meany</a>, one of the University\'s first graduates and former head of its history department. Meany and his colleague, Dean Herbert T. Condon, dubbed the columns as "Loyalty," "Industry," "Faith", and "Efficiency", or "LIFE." The columns now stand in the <a href="/wiki/Sylvan_Grove_Theater_and_Columns" title="Sylvan Grove Theater and Columns">Sylvan Grove Theater</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century_expansion">20th century expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 20th century expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Organizers of the 1909 <a href="/wiki/Alaska-Yukon-Pacific_Exposition" class="mw-redirect" title="Alaska-Yukon-Pacific Exposition">Alaska-Yukon-Pacific Exposition</a> eyed the still largely undeveloped campus as a prime setting for their <a href="/wiki/World%27s_Fair" class="mw-redirect" title="World\'s Fair">world\'s fair</a>. They came to an agreement with Washington\'s <a href="/wiki/Board_of_Regents" class="mw-redirect" title="Board of Regents">Board of Regents</a> that allowed them to use the campus grounds for the exposition. In exchange, Washington would take advantage of the campus and its development after the fair\'s conclusion. This arrangement led to a detailed site plan and several buildings, prepared in part by <a href="/wiki/John_Charles_Olmsted" title="John Charles Olmsted">John Charles Olmsted</a>. The plan was later incorporated into the overall campus master plan, permanently affecting the campus layout.</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:238px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Uwaerial1922.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Uwaerial1922.jpg/236px-Uwaerial1922.jpg" width="236" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Uwaerial1922.jpg/354px-Uwaerial1922.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Uwaerial1922.jpg/472px-Uwaerial1922.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1035" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Uwaerial1922.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nAerial view of campus, circa 1922</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Both <a href="/wiki/World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="World War">World Wars</a> brought the military to campus, with certain facilities temporarily loaned to the federal government. Regardless, subsequent post-war periods were times of dramatic growth for the University.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The period between the wars saw a significant expansion on the upper campus. Construction of the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_arts" class="mw-redirect" title="Liberal arts">liberal arts</a> <a href="/wiki/Quadrangle_(architecture)" title="Quadrangle (architecture)">quadrangle</a>, known to students as "The Quad," began in 1916 and continued to 1939. The University\'s architectural centerpiece, <a href="/wiki/Suzzallo_Library" title="Suzzallo Library">Suzzallo Library</a>, was built in 1926 and expanded in 1935. After World War II, further growth came with the <a href="/wiki/G._I._Bill_of_Rights" class="mw-redirect" title="G. I. Bill of Rights">G.I. Bill</a>. Among the most important developments of this period was the opening of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_School_of_Medicine" title="University of Washington School of Medicine">School of Medicine</a> in 1946, now consistently ranked as the top medical school in the United States. It would eventually also led to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_Medical_Center" title="University of Washington Medical Center">University of Washington Medical Center</a>, ranked by <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. News and World Report">U.S. News and World Report</a></i> to be among the top ten hospitals in the nation.</p>\n<p>During this era, many Japanese Americans were sent away to <a href="/wiki/Internment_camps" class="mw-redirect" title="Internment camps">internment camps</a> along the west coast, as part of <a href="/wiki/Executive_Order_9066" title="Executive Order 9066">Executive Order 9066</a> following the attacks on <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor" title="Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a>. Many Japanese American students and "soon-to-be" graduates were unable to receive diplomas, or be recognized for accomplishments at the university, until Washington\'s commemoration ceremony for the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Americans" title="Japanese Americans">Japanese Americans</a> entitled <a href="/wiki/The_Long_Journey_Home_(ceremonial_event)" title="The Long Journey Home (ceremonial event)">The Long Journey Home</a>, in May 2008.</p>\n<p>From 1958-1973, the University of Washington saw tremendous growth in students, faculties, operating budget, and prestige under leadership of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Odegaard" title="Charles Odegaard">Charles Odegaard</a>. UW student enrollment had more than doubled to 34,000 as the <a href="/wiki/Post-World_War_II_baby_boom" class="mw-redirect" title="Post-World War II baby boom">baby boom</a> generation came of age. However, this era was also marked by high levels of <a href="/wiki/Student_activism" title="Student activism">student activism</a>, as was the case at many American universities. Much of the unrest focused around <a href="/wiki/Civil_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil rights">civil rights</a> and opposition to the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> In response to anti-Vietnam War protests by the late 1960s, the University Safety and Security Division became the University of Washington Police Department.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Odegaard instituted a vision of building a "community of scholars", convincing the Washington State legislatures to increase their investments towards the university. Washington <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">senators</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Henry_M._Jackson" title="Henry M. Jackson">Henry M. Jackson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warren_G._Magnuson" class="mw-redirect" title="Warren G. Magnuson">Warren G. Magnuson</a>, also used their political clout to build research funds for UW. The results included an operating budget increase of $37 million in 1958 to over $400 million in 1973, and solidified UW as a top recipients of federal research funds in the United States even today. Establishment of technology giants such as <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon.com">Amazon</a> near UW has also proved to be highly influential, not only improving graduate prospects,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> but also helping to attract millions of dollars in university and research funding through its extensive list of distinguished faculty and alumni network.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:238px;"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Washington_Quad,_Spring_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/University_of_Washington_Quad%2C_Spring_2007.jpg/236px-University_of_Washington_Quad%2C_Spring_2007.jpg" width="236" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/University_of_Washington_Quad%2C_Spring_2007.jpg/354px-University_of_Washington_Quad%2C_Spring_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/University_of_Washington_Quad%2C_Spring_2007.jpg/472px-University_of_Washington_Quad%2C_Spring_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Washington_Quad,_Spring_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe Quad</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In 1990, the University of Washington opened additional campuses in <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington,_Bothell" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Washington, Bothell">Bothell</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington,_Tacoma" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Washington, Tacoma">Tacoma</a>. Although originally intended for students who have already completed two years of higher education, both schools have transitioned into four-year, degree-granting universities. The first freshman class for these campuses came in the fall of 2006, and both campuses now offer a selection master\'s degree programs as well. In 2012, the University began exploring plans and governmental approval to expand the main <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a> campus, which includes significant increases in student housing, teaching facilities for the growing student body and faculty, as well as expanded public transit options.</p>\n<p>The UW station, completed in March 2015 with six months ahead of schedule and $150 million under budget,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> connects Seattle\'s <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Hill_(Seattle)" title="Capitol Hill (Seattle)">Capitol Hill</a> to the UW Husky Stadium within 5 minutes of rail travel time.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> It represents a previously unavailable option of transportation into and out of the campus, designed specifically to reduce dependence on private vehicles, bicycles and local <a href="/wiki/King_County,_Washington" title="King County, Washington">King County</a> buses.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Campus_of_the_University_of_Washington" title="Campus of the University of Washington">Campus of the University of Washington</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:238px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Entrance_of_Suzzallo_Library.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Entrance_of_Suzzallo_Library.jpg/236px-Entrance_of_Suzzallo_Library.jpg" width="236" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Entrance_of_Suzzallo_Library.jpg/354px-Entrance_of_Suzzallo_Library.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Entrance_of_Suzzallo_Library.jpg/472px-Entrance_of_Suzzallo_Library.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Entrance_of_Suzzallo_Library.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nEntrance of the signature <a href="/wiki/Suzzallo_Library" title="Suzzallo Library">Suzzallo Library</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:238px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Meany_Hall,_University_of_Washington.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Meany_Hall%2C_University_of_Washington.jpg/236px-Meany_Hall%2C_University_of_Washington.jpg" width="236" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Meany_Hall%2C_University_of_Washington.jpg/354px-Meany_Hall%2C_University_of_Washington.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Meany_Hall%2C_University_of_Washington.jpg/472px-Meany_Hall%2C_University_of_Washington.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Meany_Hall,_University_of_Washington.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMeany Hall, concert venue, behind the <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_(Taft)" title="George Washington (Taft)">statue of George Washington</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The University of Washington main campus in Seattle is situated on the shores of <a href="/wiki/Union_Bay_(Seattle,_Washington)" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Bay (Seattle, Washington)">Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portage_Bay" title="Portage Bay">Portage Bays</a>, with views of the <a href="/wiki/Cascade_Range" title="Cascade Range">Cascade Range</a> to the east, and the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Mountains" title="Olympic Mountains">Olympic Mountains</a> to the west. It is bounded by 15th Avenue N.E. on the west, by N.E. 45th Street on the north, by Montlake Boulevard N.E. on the east, and by N.E. Pacific Street on the south.</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Red Square is the heart of the campus, surrounded by landmark buildings such as <a href="/wiki/Suzzallo_Library" title="Suzzallo Library">Suzzallo Library</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Broken_Obelisk" title="Broken Obelisk">Broken Obelisk</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_(Taft)" title="George Washington (Taft)">statue of George Washington</a>. It functions as the central hub for students, and hosts a variety of events annually.</li>\n<li>University Way, known locally as "<a href="/wiki/The_Ave" title="The Ave">The Ave</a>", lies nearby and is a focus for much student life at the university.</li>\n<li>The "East Campus" area is largely taken up by <a href="/wiki/Wetland" title="Wetland">wetlands</a> and sports fields, stretching east of Montlake Boulevard to <a href="/wiki/Laurelhurst,_Seattle,_Washington" class="mw-redirect" title="Laurelhurst, Seattle, Washington">Laurelhurst</a>.</li>\n<li>The "South Campus" occupies the land between Pacific Street and the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Washington_Ship_Canal" title="Lake Washington Ship Canal">Lake Washington Ship Canal</a>, a prior <a href="/wiki/Golf_course" title="Golf course">golf course</a> that was given over to the <a href="/wiki/Health_sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Health sciences">health sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oceanography" title="Oceanography">oceanography</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fisheries_science" title="Fisheries science">fisheries</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_Medical_Center" title="University of Washington Medical Center">University of Washington Medical Center</a>.</li>\n<li>The "West Campus" features many of its facilities being on city streets, and stretches between 15th Avenue and <a href="/wiki/Interstate_5" title="Interstate 5">Interstate 5</a> from the Ship Canal, to N.E. 41st Street.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>The campus is consistently one of the most highly regarded within the nation. Major motion pictures have either been filmed on campus or used it as a backdrop, including <i><a href="/wiki/21_and_Over_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="21 and Over (film)">21 and Over</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-21andOver_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21andOver-18">[18]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sixth_Man" class="mw-redirect" title="The Sixth Man">The Sixth Man</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-SixthMan_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SixthMan-19">[19]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/WarGames" title="WarGames">WarGames</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-WarGamesFilming_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WarGamesFilming-20">[20]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/What_the_Bleep!%3F:_Down_the_Rabbit_Hole" class="mw-redirect" title="What the Bleep!?: Down the Rabbit Hole">What the Bleep!?: Down the Rabbit Hole</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-WhatTheBleepFilming_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WhatTheBleepFilming-21">[21]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization_and_administration">Organization and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Organization and administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Washington_Presidents" class="mw-redirect" title="List of University of Washington Presidents">List of University of Washington Presidents</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>University of Washington\'s Interim President <a href="/wiki/Ana_Mari_Cauce" title="Ana Mari Cauce">Ana Mari Cauce</a> was selected president by the Board of Regents, effective October 13, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The previous President of the University of Washington was <a href="/wiki/Michael_K._Young" title="Michael K. Young">Michael K. Young</a>. <a href="/wiki/Phyllis_Wise" title="Phyllis Wise">Phyllis Wise</a>, who had previously served as Provost and Executive Vice President and for a year as Interim President, was named the Chancellor of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana-Champaign" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign">University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign</a> in August 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> On February 3, 2015, it was announced that Young will be the next President of <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_University" title="Texas A&amp;M University">Texas A&amp;M University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Regents:_Two-time_university_president_expected_to_serve_at_helm_of_Texas_A.26M_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Regents:_Two-time_university_president_expected_to_serve_at_helm_of_Texas_A.26M-24">[24]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The University is governed by ten Regents, one of whom is a student. Its most notable current regent is likely <a href="/wiki/William_H._Gates,_Sr." class="mw-redirect" title="William H. Gates, Sr.">William H. Gates, Sr.</a>, the father of <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gates" title="Bill Gates">Bill Gates</a>. The undergraduate student government is the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Students_of_the_University_of_Washington" title="Associated Students of the University of Washington">Associated Students of the University of Washington</a> (ASUW) and the graduate student government is the <a href="/wiki/Graduate_and_Professional_Student_Senate" title="Graduate and Professional Student Senate">Graduate and Professional Student Senate</a> (GPSS).</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Environmental sustainability has long been a major focus of the university\'s Board of Regents and Presidents. In February 2006, the UW joined a partnership with Seattle City Light as part of their Green Up Program, ensuring that all of Seattle campus\' electricity is supplied by and purchased from renewable sources.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> In 2010, then UW President Emmert furthered the university\'s efforts with a host of other universities across the U.S., and signed the <a href="/wiki/American_College_%26_University_Presidents%27_Climate_Commitment" title="American College &amp; University Presidents\' Climate Commitment">American College &amp; University Presidents\' Climate Commitment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> UW created a Climate Action Team,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> as well as an Environmental Stewardship Advisory Committee (ESAC) which keeps track of UW\'s greenhouse gas emissions and carbon footprint.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Policies were enacted with environmental stewardship in mind, and institutional support was provided to assist with campus sustainability.<sup id="cite_ref-Environmental_Stewardship_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Environmental_Stewardship-29">[29]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Additionally, UW\'s Student Housing and Food Services (HFS) office has dedicated several million dollars annually towards locally produced, organic, and natural foods. HFS also seized the use of styrofoam containers on-campus, and instead opted for compostable cups, plates, utensils, and packaging whenever possible. New residence halls planned for 2020 are also expected to meet silver or gold LEED standards.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Overall, the University of Washington was one of several universities to receive the highest grade, "A-", on the Sustainable Endowments Institute\'s College Sustainability Report Card in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Sustainable_Endowments_Institute_Report_Card_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sustainable_Endowments_Institute_Report_Card-31">[31]</a></sup> The University was one of 15 Overall College Sustainability Leaders, among the 300 institutions surveyed.<sup id="cite_ref-uwnews.org_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uwnews.org-32">[32]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics_and_research">Academics and research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Academics and research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:238px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mary_Gates_Hall_at_the_UW_in_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Mary_Gates_Hall_at_the_UW_in_2006.jpg/236px-Mary_Gates_Hall_at_the_UW_in_2006.jpg" width="236" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Mary_Gates_Hall_at_the_UW_in_2006.jpg/354px-Mary_Gates_Hall_at_the_UW_in_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Mary_Gates_Hall_at_the_UW_in_2006.jpg/472px-Mary_Gates_Hall_at_the_UW_in_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mary_Gates_Hall_at_the_UW_in_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nInterior of the <a href="/wiki/Mary_Maxwell_Gates" title="Mary Maxwell Gates">Mary Gates</a> Hall</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The University offers bachelor\'s, master\'s and <a href="/wiki/Doctoral_degree" class="mw-redirect" title="Doctoral degree">doctoral</a> degrees through its 140 departments, themselves organized into various colleges and schools:<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>\n<table>\n<tr>\n<td valign="top">\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_College_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="University of Washington College of Arts and Sciences">College of Arts and Sciences</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_Henry_M._Jackson_School_of_International_Studies" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Washington Henry M. Jackson School of International Studies">Henry M. Jackson School of International Studies</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_College_of_Built_Environments" title="University of Washington College of Built Environments">College of Built Environments</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_Business_School" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Washington Business School">Michael G. Foster School of Business</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_School_of_Dentistry" title="University of Washington School of Dentistry">School of Dentistry</a></li>\n<li>College of Education</li>\n<li>College of Engineering</li>\n<li>Paul G. Allen School of Computer Science &amp; Engineering</li>\n<li>College of the Environment</li>\n<li>The Graduate School</li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n<td valign="top">\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_Information_School" title="University of Washington Information School">Information School</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_School_of_Law" title="University of Washington School of Law">School of Law</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_School_of_Medicine" title="University of Washington School of Medicine">School of Medicine</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_School_of_Nursing" title="University of Washington School of Nursing">School of Nursing</a></li>\n<li>School of Oceanography</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_School_of_Pharmacy" title="University of Washington School of Pharmacy">School of Pharmacy</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Daniel_J._Evans_School_of_Public_Policy_and_Governance" title="Daniel J. Evans School of Public Policy and Governance">Daniel J. Evans School of Public Policy and Governance</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_School_of_Public_Health" title="University of Washington School of Public Health">School of Public Health</a></li>\n<li>School of Social Work</li>\n<li>School of Aquatic and Fishery Sciences</li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>The University of Washington recruits faculty and staff from around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Among the faculty, there are 151 members of American Association for the Advancement of Science, 68 members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academy_of_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="United States National Academy of Sciences">National Academy of Sciences</a>, 67 members of the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>, 53 members of the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Medicine" class="mw-redirect" title="Institute of Medicine">Institute of Medicine</a>, 7 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> laureates, 2 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners, 1 winner of the <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medal</a>, 21 members of the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Engineering" title="National Academy of Engineering">National Academy of Engineering</a>, 1 member of the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Public_Administration_(United_States)" title="National Academy of Public Administration (United States)">National Academy of Public Administration</a>, 29 winners of the Presidential Early Career Awards in Science and Engineering, 15 Howard Hughes Medical Institute Investigators, 15 <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Fellows" class="mw-redirect" title="MacArthur Fellows">MacArthur Fellows</a>, 9 winners of the <a href="/wiki/Gairdner_Foundation_International_Award" title="Gairdner Foundation International Award">Gairdner Foundation International Award</a>, 5 winners of the <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Science" title="National Medal of Science">National Medal of Science</a>, 5 winners of <a href="/wiki/Albert_Lasker_Award_for_Clinical_Medical_Research" class="mw-redirect" title="Albert Lasker Award for Clinical Medical Research">Albert Lasker Award for Clinical Medical Research</a>, 4 members of the <a href="/wiki/American_Philosophical_Society" title="American Philosophical Society">American Philosophical Society</a>, 2 winners of the <a href="/wiki/National_Book_Award" title="National Book Award">National Book Award</a>, and 2 winners of the <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Arts" class="mw-redirect" title="National Medal of Arts">National Medal of Arts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> By 2012, UW students include 136 Fulbright Scholars, 35 Rhodes Scholars, 7 Marshall Scholars and 4 Gates Cambridge Scholars.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div style="float:right; font-size:85%: text-align:center;"></div>\n<p>Since 1977, the University of Washington has operated a <a href="/wiki/Transition_School_and_Early_Entrance_Program" title="Transition School and Early Entrance Program">Transition School and Early Entrance Program</a> on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-eep_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eep-38">[38]</a></sup> The university\'s undergraduate admissions process is rated at 91/99 by the <a href="/wiki/Princeton_Review" class="mw-redirect" title="Princeton Review">Princeton Review</a> meaning highly selective,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> and is classified as "more selective" by the <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> For students entering Fall 2016, 19,733 were accepted out of 43,517 applications - a 45.3% acceptance rate. 6,475 of the admitted students enrolled.<sup id="cite_ref-QuickFacts_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QuickFacts-42">[42]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Among freshman students who enrolled in fall 2016, <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> scores for admitted students ranged from 1210-1420. More specifically, the middle 50% scores ranged from 610-700 for evidence-based reading and writing, and 600\xe2\x80\x93740 for math.<sup id="cite_ref-QuickFacts_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QuickFacts-42">[42]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ACT_(examination)" class="mw-redirect" title="ACT (examination)">ACT</a> composite scores for the middle 50% ranged from 26\xe2\x80\x9332.<sup id="cite_ref-QuickFacts_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QuickFacts-42">[42]</a></sup> The middle 50% of high school <a href="/wiki/GPA" class="mw-redirect" title="GPA">GPA</a> ranged from 3.68\xe2\x80\x933.94, out of typically 4.0.<sup id="cite_ref-QuickFacts_42-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QuickFacts-42">[42]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings_and_reputation">Rankings and reputation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Rankings and reputation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width: 22em">\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2" style="text-align: center; font-size: 125%"><a href="/wiki/College_and_university_rankings" title="College and university rankings">University rankings</a></th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2" style="background-color: lavender; text-align: center">National</th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th><i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">ARWU</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_ARWU_NU_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_ARWU_NU-43">[43]</a></sup></th>\n<td>11</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th><i><a href="/wiki/Forbes_Magazine%27s_List_of_America%27s_Best_Colleges" title="Forbes Magazine\'s List of America\'s Best Colleges">Forbes</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_Forbes_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_Forbes-44">[44]</a></sup></th>\n<td>79</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th><i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_USNWR_NU_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_USNWR_NU-45">[45]</a></sup></th>\n<td>54</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th><i><a href="/wiki/Washington_Monthly" title="Washington Monthly">Washington Monthly</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_Wamo_NU_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_Wamo_NU-46">[46]</a></sup></th>\n<td>8</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2" style="background-color: lavender; text-align: center">Global</th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th><i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">ARWU</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_ARWU_W_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_ARWU_W-47">[47]</a></sup></th>\n<td>13</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th><i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_QS_W_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_QS_W-48">[48]</a></sup></th>\n<td>61</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th><i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_THES_W_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_THES_W-49">[49]</a></sup></th>\n<td>25</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th><i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_USNWR_W_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_USNWR_W-50">[50]</a></sup></th>\n<td>11</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Washington is a globally recognized flagship university, as reflected in its strong performance across rankings. It was listed as a "<a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">Public Ivy</a>" in <a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy#Greenes.27_Guides" title="Public Ivy">Greene\'s Guides</a> since 2001,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> and is an elected member of the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_of_Universities" class="mw-redirect" title="American Association of Universities">American Association of Universities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> (ARWU)</i> has consistently ranked UW as one of the top 20 universities worldwide every year since its first release.<sup id="cite_ref-shanghairanking1_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shanghairanking1-53">[53]</a></sup> In 2017, UW ranked 13th worldwide out of 500 by the <i>ARWU</i>, 25th worldwide out of 981 in the <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings"><i>Times Higher Education World University Rankings</i></a>, and 26th worldwide out of 101 in the <i>Times</i> <a href="/wiki/World_Reputation_Rankings" class="mw-redirect" title="World Reputation Rankings">World Reputation Rankings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Meanwhile, <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings"><i>QS World University Rankings</i></a> ranked it 59th worldwide, out of over 900.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report"><i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i></a>\'s Best Global Universities ranked UW as top 11th worldwide, out of 1,000 in 2017. Nationally, UW\'s undergraduate program was tied for 54th out of 310, and among public universities was tied for 16th out of 133. As for graduate programs, UW was ranked as follows in 2017:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Best in primary care and family medicine,</li>\n<li>2nd best in <a href="/wiki/Library_and_information_sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Library and information sciences">library and information sciences</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clinical_psychology" title="Clinical psychology">clinical psychology</a>,</li>\n<li>3rd best in <a href="/wiki/Social_work" title="Social work">social work</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biostatistics" title="Biostatistics">biostatistics</a>,</li>\n<li>4th best in public affairs, and</li>\n<li>6th best in <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nursing" title="Nursing">nursing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a></li>\n</ul>\n<p>Other nationally competitive UW graduate programs include statistics at 7th, pharmacy and education at 9th, engineering at 25th, business at 27th, and law at 30th \xe2\x80\x94 also referred to as a competitive "Tier 1" school.<sup id="cite_ref-USNWR_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNWR-6">[6]</a></sup></p>\n<p>As for other rankings: In 2010, <i>Top American Research Universities</i>, published by <a href="/wiki/The_Center_for_Measuring_University_Performance" class="mw-redirect" title="The Center for Measuring University Performance">The Center for Measuring University Performance</a> of <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University" title="Arizona State University">Arizona State University</a>, ranked the University of Washington 11th among the top 50 American universities.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> In 2011, UW was ranked 8th globally among 2,000 universities in <i><a href="/wiki/University_Ranking_by_Academic_Performance" title="University Ranking by Academic Performance">University Ranking by Academic Performance</a> (URAP)</i> published by <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Technical_University" title="Middle East Technical University">Middle East Technical University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> <i>Top 200 Colleges and Universities in the World</i>, published by 4 international colleges and universities, ranked UW at 8th globally in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> In 2017, the <a href="/wiki/CWTS_Leiden_Ranking" title="CWTS Leiden Ranking"><i>Leiden Ranking</i></a>, which focuses on science and the impact of scientific publications among the world\'s 500 major universities, ranked UW 12th globally and 5th in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Washington is also recognized in more specific domains. In 2012, the <a href="/wiki/SmartMoney" title="SmartMoney"><i>Wall Street Journal</i>\'s <i>SmartMoney</i></a> named UW 6th best in salary returns on tuition.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> In 2014, <i><a href="/wiki/Kiplinger" title="Kiplinger">Kiplinger</a></i> magazine\'s "Best Values in Public Colleges" named UW 11th for in-state students, and 28th for out-of-state students.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> In 2012, the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Peace_Corps" title="Peace Corps">Peace Corps</a> ranked UW 2nd among large U.S. universities, based on the number of undergraduate alumni serving as volunteers.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> In the <i><a href="/wiki/Washington_Monthly" title="Washington Monthly">Washington Monthly</a></i> National University Rankings, UW was ranked 8th domestically in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The University of Washington research budget passed its $1.0 billion milestone in 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-UW_.241_billion_research_mark_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UW_.241_billion_research_mark-64">[64]</a></sup> and endowments reached almost $3.0 billion by 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> As a large flagship university, UW\'s research budget consistently ranks among the top 5 in both public and private universities in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-UW_Annual_Report_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UW_Annual_Report-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-top_research_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top_research-67">[67]</a></sup> UW is also the largest recipient of federal research funding among public universities, and 2nd among all public and private universities in the country: a position held since 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>\n<p>To promote equal academic opportunity, especially for people of low income, UW launched <i>Husky Promise</i> in 2006. Families of income up to 65 percent of state median income or 235 percent of federal poverty level are eligible. With this, up to 30 percent of undergraduate students may be eligible. The cut-off income level that UW set is the highest in the nation, making top quality education available to more people. Then UW President, Mark Emmert, simply said that being "elitist is not in our DNA".<sup id="cite_ref-Inside_HigherEd_Husky_Promise_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inside_HigherEd_Husky_Promise-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UW_Husky_Promise_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UW_Husky_Promise-70">[70]</a></sup> "Last year, the University of Washington moved to a more comprehensive approach [to admissions], in which the admissions staff reads the entire application and looks at grades within the context of the individual high school, rather than relying on computerized cutoffs."<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>\n<p>UW was the host university of <a href="/wiki/ResearchChannel" class="mw-redirect" title="ResearchChannel">ResearchChannel</a> program (now defunct), the only TV channel in the United States dedicated solely for the dissemination of research from academic institutions and research organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-ResearchChannel_host_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ResearchChannel_host-72">[72]</a></sup> Participation of ResearchChannel included 36 universities, 15 research organizations, two corporate research centers and many other affiliates.<sup id="cite_ref-ResearchChannel_participants_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ResearchChannel_participants-73">[73]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 2014, teams from the University of Washington School of Oceanography and the UW Applied Physics Laboratory successfully completed construction of the first <a href="/wiki/Regional_Scale_Nodes" title="Regional Scale Nodes">high-power underwater cabled observatory</a> in the United States.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center; float:right; font-size:85%; margin-left:2em; margin:10px">\n<caption><i>Demographics of student body (Spring 2014)</i><sup id="cite_ref-WashStats_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashStats-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></caption>\n<tr>\n<th></th>\n<th>Student Body</th>\n<th>Washington</th>\n<th>U.S. Census</th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/African_American" class="mw-redirect" title="African American">African American</a></th>\n<td>3.42%</td>\n<td>3.6%</td>\n<td>12.0%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Asian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian American">Asian American</a></th>\n<td>22.8%</td>\n<td>7.2%</td>\n<td>4.7%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/White_American" class="mw-redirect" title="White American">White American</a></th>\n<td>48.0%</td>\n<td>72.5%</td>\n<td>63.7%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Hispanics_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Hispanics in the United States">Hispanic American</a></th>\n<td>6.4%</td>\n<td>4.8%</td>\n<td>16.3%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native American</a></th>\n<td>1.3%</td>\n<td>1.5%</td>\n<td>0.7%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/International_student" title="International student">International student</a></th>\n<td>14.3%</td>\n<td>N/A</td>\n<td>N/A</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Other/Unknown</th>\n<td>3.1%</td>\n<td>5.2%</td>\n<td>2.4%</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>As of the 2016\xe2\x80\x9317 autumn quarter, the university had 46,081 total enrollments, making it the largest university (in terms of student population) on the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="West Coast of the United States">west coast</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> About 33% of all undergraduates are members of <a href="/wiki/Minority_group" title="Minority group">minority groups</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organizations">Organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Organizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Registered_groups">Registered groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Registered groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The University of Washington boasts over 800 active Registered Student Organizations (RSOs), one of the largest networks of any universities in the world. RSOs are dedicated to a wide variety of interests both in and beyond campus. Some of these interest areas include academic focus groups, cultural exchanges, environmental activities, Greek life, political/social action, religious discussions, sports, international student gatherings by country, and STEM-specific events. Prominent examples are:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><b>The Dream Project</b>: "The Dream Project teaches UW students to mentor first-generation and low-income students in King County high schools as they navigate the complex college-admissions process."<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>The Rural Health Education (RHE)</b>: Promotes health in rural areas of Washington state through health fairs. Volunteers include students from a variety of backgrounds including: medical, pharmacy, and dentistry. Health professionals from the Greater Seattle area also actively participate.</li>\n<li><b>Students Expressing Environmental Concern (SEED)</b>: partially funded by UW\'s Housing and Food Services (HFS) office to promote environmental sustainability, and reduce the university\'s carbon footprint.</li>\n<li><b>Student Philanthropy Education Program</b>: Partnered with the UW\'s nonprofit, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.washington.edu/giving/">UW Foundation</a>, this group focuses on promoting awareness of philanthropy\'s importance through major events on campus.</li>\n<li><b>UW Delta Delta Sigma Pre-Dental Society (DDS)</b>: This is a club dedicated to serving pre-dental students and it provides a forum for discussion of dental related topics.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>UW Earth Club</b>: The Earth Club is interested in promoting the expression of environmental attitudes and consciousness through specialized events.</li>\n<li><b>UW Farm</b>: The UW farm grows crops on campus and advocates urban farming in the UW community.</li>\n<li><b>GlobeMed at UW</b>: a student-run non-profit organization that works to educate about global poverty and its effect on health. The UW chapter is a part of a national network of chapters, each partnering with a grassroots organization at home or abroad. GlobeMed at UW is partnered with <a href="/wiki/The_MINDS_Foundation" title="The MINDS Foundation">The MINDS Foundation</a> which supports education about and treatment for mental illness in rural India.</li>\n<li><b>UW Sierra Student Coalition</b>: SSC is dedicated to many larger environmental issues on campus and providing related opportunities to students.</li>\n<li><b>Washington Public Interest Research Group (WashPIRG)</b>: WashPIRG engages students in a variety of activism causes, including environmental projects on campus and the community.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></li>\n</ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_government">Student government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Student government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Associated_Students_of_the_University_of_Washington" title="Associated Students of the University of Washington">Associated Students of the University of Washington</a></div>\n<p>The Associated Students of the University of Washington (ASUW) is one of two Student Governments at the University of Washington, the other being the Graduate and Professional Student Senate. It is funded and supported by student fees, and provides services that directly and indirectly benefit them. The ASUW employs over 72 current University of Washington students, has over 500 volunteers, and spends $1.03 million annually to provide services and activities to the student body of 43,000 on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> The Student Senate was established in 1994 as a division of the Associated Students of the University of Washington. Student Senate is one of two official student governed bodies and provides a broad-based discussion of issues. Currently, the ASUW Student Senate has a legislative body of over 150 senators representing a diverse set of interests on and off campus.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The ASUW was incorporated in the State of Washington on April 20, 1906.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> On April 30, 1932 the ASUW assisted in the incorporation of the University Bookstore<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> which has been in continuous operation at the same location on University Way for over 70 years. The <a href="/wiki/ASUW_Experimental_College" class="mw-redirect" title="ASUW Experimental College">ASUW Experimental College</a>, part of the ASUW, was created in 1968 by several University of Washington students seeking to provide the campus and surrounding community with a selection of classes not offered on the university curriculum.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Publication">Publication</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Publication">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Daily_of_the_University_of_Washington" title="The Daily of the University of Washington">The Daily of the University of Washington</a></div>\n<p>The student newspaper is <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_of_the_University_of_Washington" title="The Daily of the University of Washington">The Daily of the University of Washington</a></i>, usually referred to as <i>The Daily</i>. It is an award-winning publication, and is the second largest daily in Seattle. <i>The Daily</i> is published every day classes are in session during fall, winter and spring quarters, as well as weekly during summer quarters. In 2010, <i>The Daily</i> launched a half-hour weekly television magazine show, "The Daily\'s Double Shot," on <a href="/wiki/UWTV" class="mw-redirect" title="UWTV">UWTV</a> Channel 27.</p>\n<p>Today, UW continues to disseminate knowledge through its proprietary <a href="/wiki/UWTV" class="mw-redirect" title="UWTV">UWTV</a> channel, online and printed publications.<sup id="cite_ref-UWTV_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UWTV-87">[87]</a></sup> Specific faculties also produce their own publications for students and alumni.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Support">Support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Support">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UW_Tower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/UW_Tower.jpg/190px-UW_Tower.jpg" width="190" height="285" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/UW_Tower.jpg/285px-UW_Tower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/UW_Tower.jpg/380px-UW_Tower.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2602" data-file-height="3906" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UW_Tower.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/UW_Tower" title="UW Tower">UW Tower</a>, conference space and administrative building</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>UW offers many services for its students and alumni, beyond the standard offered by most colleges and universities. Its "Student Life" division houses 16 departments and offices that serve students directly and indirectly, including those below and overseen by Vice President and Vice Provost.</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Career Center</li>\n<li>Counseling Center</li>\n<li>Department of Recreational Sports (IMA)</li>\n<li>Disability Resource Center</li>\n<li>Fraternity and Sorority Life</li>\n<li>Health and Wellness Programs</li>\n<li>Housing and Food Services</li>\n<li>Office of Ceremonies</li>\n<li>Office of the University Registrar</li>\n<li>Student Admissions</li>\n<li>Student Activities and Union Facilities</li>\n<li>Student Financial Aid</li>\n<li>Student Legal Services</li>\n<li>Student Publications (The Daily)</li>\n<li>Campus Police<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></li>\n</ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Housing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The University operates one of the largest campuses of any higher education institutions in the world. Despite so, growing faculty and student count has strained the regional housing supply as well as transportation facilities. Starting in 2012, UW began taking active measures to explore, plan and enact a series of campus policies to manage the annual growth. In addition to new buildings, parking and light rail stations, new building construction and renovations have been scheduled to take place through 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> The plan includes the construction of three six-story residence halls and two apartment complexes in the west section of campus, near the existing <a href="/wiki/Terry_and_Lander_Halls" title="Terry and Lander Halls">Terry and Lander Halls</a>, in Phase I, the renovation of six existing residence halls in Phase II, and additional new construction in Phase III. The projects will result in a net gain of approximately 2,400 beds. The Residence Hall Student Association (student government for the halls) is the second largest student organization on campus and helps plan fun events in the halls. For students, faculty, and staff looking to live off-campus, they may also explore Off-Campus Housing Affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The Greek System at UW has also been a prominent part of student culture for more than 115 years. It is made up of two organizational bodies, the Interfraternity Council (IFC) and the Panhellenic Association. The IFC looks over 34 fraternities with 1900+ members and Panhellenic consists of 19 sororities and 1900 members. The school has additional Greek organizations that do not offer housing and are primarily special interest.</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Disabilities">Disabilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Disabilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/The_DO-IT_Center" title="The DO-IT Center">DO-IT (Disabilities, Opportunities, Internetworking, and Technology) Center</a> is a program run by the university which assists educational institutions to fully integrate all students, including those with disabilities, into Academic life. DO-IT runs many programs, including the <a href="/wiki/DO-IT_Scholars_Program" title="DO-IT Scholars Program">DO-IT Scholars Program</a>, and a database of information on the \'universal\' design of educational facilities for students of all levels of physical and mental ability.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> These design programs reduce systemic barriers which could otherwise hinder the performance of some students. DO-IT\'s universal design philosophies may also be applied to professional organizations and conferences.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Washington_Huskies" title="Washington Huskies">Washington Huskies</a></div>\n<p>The sports teams participate in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a>\'s Division I-A and in the <a href="/wiki/Pac-12_Conference" title="Pac-12 Conference">Pac-12 Conference</a>. Among its facilities on campus are <a href="/wiki/Husky_Stadium" title="Husky Stadium">Husky Stadium</a> (football, track and field), the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Airlines_Arena_at_Hec_Edmundson_Pavilion" class="mw-redirect" title="Alaska Airlines Arena at Hec Edmundson Pavilion">Alaska Airlines Arena at Hec Edmundson Pavilion</a> (basketball, volleyball, and gymnastics), <a href="/wiki/Husky_Ballpark" title="Husky Ballpark">Husky Ballpark</a> (baseball), Husky Softball Stadium, The <a href="/wiki/William_Quillian_(athlete)" class="mw-redirect" title="William Quillian (athlete)">Bill Quillian Tennis Stadium</a>, The <a href="/wiki/Nordstrom" title="Nordstrom">Nordstrom</a> Tennis Center, Dempsey Indoor (Indoor track and field, football) and the <a href="/wiki/Conibear_Shellhouse" title="Conibear Shellhouse">Conibear Shellhouse</a> (rowing). The golf team plays at the Washington National Golf Club and until recently, the swimming team called the <a href="/wiki/Weyerhaeuser" title="Weyerhaeuser">Weyerhaeuser</a> Aquatic Center and the Husky pool home. (The university eliminated its men\'s and women\'s swim teams in May 2009.)<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Washington_Huskies_football" title="Washington Huskies football">football team</a> is traditionally competitive, having won the 1960 and 1991 national title, to go along with eight <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_(game)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rose Bowl (game)">Rose Bowl</a> victories and an <a href="/wiki/Orange_Bowl_(game)" class="mw-redirect" title="Orange Bowl (game)">Orange Bowl</a> title. From 1907 to 1917, Washington football teams were unbeaten in 64 consecutive games, an <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> record.<sup id="cite_ref-unbeaten_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unbeaten-94">[94]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tailgate_party" title="Tailgate party">Tailgating</a> by boat has been a Husky Stadium tradition since 1920 when the stadium was first built on the shores of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Washington" title="Lake Washington">Lake Washington</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Apple_Cup" title="Apple Cup">Apple Cup</a> game is an annual game against cross-state rival <a href="/wiki/Washington_State_University" title="Washington State University">Washington State University</a> that was first contested in 1900 with UW leading the all-time series, 65 wins to 31 losses and 6 ties. <a href="/wiki/College_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="College Football Hall of Fame">College Football Hall of Fame</a> member <a href="/wiki/Don_James_(American_football)" title="Don James (American football)">Don James</a> is a former head coach.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:238px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hec_Ed.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Hec_Ed.JPG/236px-Hec_Ed.JPG" width="236" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Hec_Ed.JPG/354px-Hec_Ed.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Hec_Ed.JPG/472px-Hec_Ed.JPG 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hec_Ed.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Alaska_Airlines_Arena_at_Hec_Edmundson_Pavilion" class="mw-redirect" title="Alaska Airlines Arena at Hec Edmundson Pavilion">Hec Edmundson Pavilion</a><br />\nhosts basketball and volleyball</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The men\'s <a href="/wiki/Washington_Huskies_men%27s_basketball" title="Washington Huskies men\'s basketball">basketball</a> team has been moderately successful, though recently the team has enjoyed a resurgence under coach <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Romar" title="Lorenzo Romar">Lorenzo Romar</a>. With Romar as head coach, the team has been to six <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="NCAA Men\'s Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA tournaments</a> (2003\xe2\x80\x932004, 2004\xe2\x80\x932005, 2005\xe2\x80\x932006, 2008\xe2\x80\x932009, 2009\xe2\x80\x932010 and 2010\xe2\x80\x932011 seasons), 2 consecutive top 16 (sweet sixteen) appearances, and secured a No. 1 seed in 2005. On December 23, 2005, the men\'s basketball team won their 800th victory in Hec Edmundson Pavilion, the most wins for any NCAA team in its current arena.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/College_rowing_(United_States)" title="College rowing (United States)">Rowing</a> is a longstanding tradition at the University of Washington dating back to 1901. The Washington men\'s crew gained international prominence by winning the <a href="/wiki/Gold_medal" title="Gold medal">gold medal</a> at the <a href="/wiki/1936_Summer_Olympics" title="1936 Summer Olympics">1936 Summer Olympics</a> in Berlin, defeating the German and Italian crews much to the dismay of <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> who was in attendance.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> In 1958, the men\'s crew deepened their legend with a shocking win over <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Leningrad</a> Trud\'s world champion rowers at the Moscow Cup, resulting in the first American sporting victory on <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> soil,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> and certainly the first time a <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian</a> crowd gave any American team a standing ovation during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> The men\'s crew have won 46 national titles<sup id="cite_ref-RowingSuccessful_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RowingSuccessful-99">[99]</a></sup> (15 <a href="/wiki/Intercollegiate_Rowing_Association" title="Intercollegiate Rowing Association">Intercollegiate Rowing Association</a>, 1 <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Rowing_Championship" title="National Collegiate Rowing Championship">National Collegiate Rowing Championship</a>), 15 Olympic gold medals, two silver and five bronze. The women have 10 national titles and two Olympic gold medals.
