In 1997, the women\'s team won the NCAA championship.<sup id="cite_ref-RowingSuccessful_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RowingSuccessful-99">[99]</a></sup> The Husky men are the 2015 national champions.</p>\n<p>Recent national champions include the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Huskies_softball" title="Washington Huskies softball">softball</a> team (<a href="/wiki/2009_Women%27s_College_World_Series" title="2009 Women\'s College World Series">2009</a>), the men\'s rowing team (2015, 2014, 2013, 2012, 2011, 2009, 2007), NCAA Division I women\'s <a href="/wiki/Cross_country_running" title="Cross country running">cross country</a> team (2008), and the women\'s volleyball team (<a href="/wiki/2005_NCAA_Division_I_Women%27s_Volleyball_Tournament" title="2005 NCAA Division I Women\'s Volleyball Tournament">2005</a>). Individually, Scott Roth was the 2011 NCAA men\'s Outdoor <a href="/wiki/Pole_Vault" class="mw-redirect" title="Pole Vault">Pole Vault</a> and 2011 &amp; 2010 NCAA men\'s Indoor Pole Vault champion. <a href="/wiki/James_Lepp" title="James Lepp">James Lepp</a> was the 2005 NCAA men\'s golf champion. Ryan Brown (men\'s 800 meters) and Amy Lia (women\'s 1500 meters) won individual titles at the 2006 NCAA Track and Field Championships. <a href="/wiki/Brad_Walker_(athlete)" title="Brad Walker (athlete)">Brad Walker</a> was the 2005 NCAA men\'s Outdoor and Indoor Pole Vault champion.</p>\n<p>Husky Stadium is one of several places that may have been the birthplace of the crowd phenomenon known as "<a href="/wiki/Audience_wave" class="mw-redirect" title="Audience wave">The Wave</a>". It is claimed that the wave was invented in October 1981 by Husky graduate Robb Weller and UW band director Bill Bissel. Their opponent that afternoon was Stanford.</p>\n<p>On May 1, 2009, the athletic department announced it was discontinuing both men\'s and women\'s swimming programs effective immediately due to budget cuts.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Husky_Stadium">Husky Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Husky Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:239px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alberg_pano_piece_04.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Alberg_pano_piece_04.jpg/237px-Alberg_pano_piece_04.jpg" width="237" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Alberg_pano_piece_04.jpg/356px-Alberg_pano_piece_04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Alberg_pano_piece_04.jpg/474px-Alberg_pano_piece_04.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alberg_pano_piece_04.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nLake Washington view, from campus side</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Husky_Stadium" title="Husky Stadium">Husky Stadium</a></div>\n<p>The renovated Husky Stadium is the first and primary income source of a completely remodeled athletic district. This major remodel of the athletic village will take decades to complete, as it will take place at the same time as a massive project by the Washington State Department of Transportation on nearby highways and bridges. The stadium project consists of a new grand concourse, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_station" title="University of Washington station">underground light-rail station</a> (opened March 19, 2016<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup>), enclosed west end of the stadium, replacement of bleachers with individual seating, removal of track and Huskytron, new press box, private box seating, lowering of the field, football offices, permanent seating in the east end zone that does not block the view of Lake Washington, and new and improved amenities, concession stands and bathrooms throughout. The cost for renovating the stadium was around $280 million with a <a href="/wiki/Seating_capacity" title="Seating capacity">seating capacity</a> slightly lower than previous, at 70,138 seats. Husky Stadium is used for Graduation.</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot">Mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Mascot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Basketball_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Basketball_1.JPG/190px-Basketball_1.JPG" width="190" height="253" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Basketball_1.JPG/285px-Basketball_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Basketball_1.JPG/379px-Basketball_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2112" data-file-height="2816" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Basketball_1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe previous costumed Harry the Husky at a school basketball game.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harry_the_Husky" title="Harry the Husky">Harry the Husky</a></div>\n<p>UW students, sports teams, and alumni are called <a href="/wiki/Washington_Huskies" title="Washington Huskies">Washington Huskies</a>, and often referred to <a href="/wiki/Metonymy" title="Metonymy">metonymically</a> as "Montlake," due to the campus\'s location on Montlake Boulevard N.E.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> (although the traditional bounds of the <a href="/wiki/Montlake,_Seattle,_Washington" class="mw-redirect" title="Montlake, Seattle, Washington">Montlake neighborhood</a> do not extend north of the <a href="/wiki/Montlake_Cut" title="Montlake Cut">Montlake Cut</a> to include the campus.) The <a href="/wiki/Husky" title="Husky">husky</a> was selected as the school mascot by student committee in 1922. It replaced the "Sun Dodger," an abstract reference to the <a href="/wiki/Seattle,_Washington#Climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Seattle, Washington">local weather</a> that was quickly dropped in favor of something more tangible. The costumed "Harry the Husky" performs at sporting and special events, and a live <a href="/wiki/Alaskan_Malamute" title="Alaskan Malamute">Alaskan Malamute</a>, currently named Dubs, has traditionally led the UW <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> team onto the field at the start of games. The school colors of purple and gold were adopted in 1892 by student vote. The choice was inspired by the first <a href="/wiki/Stanza" title="Stanza">stanza</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lord_Byron" title="Lord Byron">Lord Byron</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Destruction_of_Sennacherib" title="The Destruction of Sennacherib">The Destruction of Sennacherib</a></i>:<sup id="cite_ref-SchoolColors_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SchoolColors-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>\n<blockquote>\n<div class="poem">\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">Assyrian</a> came down like the wolf on the fold,<br />\nAnd his cohorts were gleaming in purple and gold;<br />\nAnd the sheen of their spears was like stars on the sea,<br />\nWhen the blue wave rolls nightly on deep <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Galilee" title="Sea of Galilee">Galilee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SchoolColors_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SchoolColors-103">[103]</a></sup></p>\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n<p>The University of Washington\'s costumed mascot is <a href="/wiki/Harry_the_Husky" title="Harry the Husky">Harry the Husky</a>.</p>\n<p>The University of Washington has also hosted a long line of <a href="/wiki/Alaskan_Malamute" title="Alaskan Malamute">Alaskan Malamutes</a> as mascots. The 13 dogs thus far have been:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Frosty I (1922\xe2\x80\x9329)</li>\n<li>Frosty II (1930\xe2\x80\x9336)</li>\n<li>Wasky (1946)</li>\n<li>Wasky II (1947\xe2\x80\x9353)</li>\n<li>Ski (1954\xe2\x80\x9357)</li>\n<li>Denali (1958)</li>\n<li>King Chinook (1959\xe2\x80\x9368)</li>\n<li>Regent Denali (1969\xe2\x80\x9380)</li>\n<li>Sundodger (1981\xe2\x80\x9391)</li>\n<li>King Redoubt (1992\xe2\x80\x9397)</li>\n<li>Prince Redoubt (1998)</li>\n<li>Spirit (1999\xe2\x80\x932008)</li>\n<li>Dubs (2009\xe2\x80\x93 )</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Originally the dogs were cared for by the <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Alpha_Epsilon" title="Sigma Alpha Epsilon">Sigma Alpha Epsilon</a> fraternity, followed by a 49-year tradition (1959\xe2\x80\x932008) of care by the Cross family (a UW professor followed by his son).</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Song">Song</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Song">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_Husky_Marching_Band" title="University of Washington Husky Marching Band">University of Washington Husky Marching Band</a> performs at many Husky sporting events including all <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> games. The band was founded in 1929, and today it is a cornerstone of Husky spirit. The band marches using a traditional high step, and it is one of only a few marching bands left in the United States to do so. Like many college bands, the Husky band has several traditional songs that it has played for decades, including the official <a href="/wiki/Fight_song" title="Fight song">fight songs</a> "<a href="/wiki/Bow_Down_to_Washington" title="Bow Down to Washington">Bow Down to Washington</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Tequila_(song)" title="Tequila (song)">Tequila</a>", as well as fan-favorite "Africano".</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni_and_faculty">Notable alumni and faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Notable alumni and faculty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Washington_people" title="List of University of Washington people">List of University of Washington people</a></div>\n<p>Notable alumni of the University of Washington include U.S. Olympic rower <a href="/wiki/Joe_Rantz" title="Joe Rantz">Joe Rantz</a> (1936); architect <a href="/wiki/Minoru_Yamasaki" title="Minoru Yamasaki">Minoru Yamasaki</a> (1934); US Senator <a href="/wiki/Henry_M._Jackson" title="Henry M. Jackson">Henry M. Jackson</a> (JD 1935); Baskin &amp; Robbins co-founder <a href="/wiki/Irv_Robbins" title="Irv Robbins">Irv Robbins</a> (1939); former actor, <a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a> columnist and <a href="/wiki/Turner_Classic_Movies" title="Turner Classic Movies">TCM</a> host <a href="/wiki/Robert_Osborne" title="Robert Osborne">Robert Osborne</a> (1954); glass artist <a href="/wiki/Dale_Chihuly" title="Dale Chihuly">Dale Chihuly</a> (BA 1965); <a href="/wiki/Serial_killer" title="Serial killer">Serial killer</a> <a href="/wiki/Ted_Bundy" title="Ted Bundy">Ted Bundy</a> (BA, Psychology 1972); Pulitzer Prize-winning author <a href="/wiki/Marilynne_Robinson" title="Marilynne Robinson">Marilynne Robinson</a> (PhD 1977), martial artist <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Lee" title="Bruce Lee">Bruce Lee</a>; saxophonist <a href="/wiki/Kenny_G" title="Kenny G">Kenny G</a> (1978); MySpace co-founder <a href="/wiki/Chris_DeWolfe" title="Chris DeWolfe">Chris DeWolfe</a> (1988); actor <a href="/wiki/Tom_Choi" title="Tom Choi">Tom Choi</a> (BA, Drama); and actor and comedian <a href="/wiki/Joel_McHale" title="Joel McHale">Joel McHale</a> (1995, MFA 2000).</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_film">In film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
